But did Rebbi Tarphon, the teacher of all of Israel, not err between blowing for assembly and the blowing for a sacrifice? As it is written: <i>The descendants of Aaron</i>, <i>the priests, shall blow the trumpets</i><sup class="footnote-marker">178</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:8" href="/Numbers.10.8"><i>Num</i>. 10:8</a>.</i>, blameless ones, not with bodily defects, the words of Rebbi Aqiba. Rebbi Tarphon said to him, I would hit my sons<sup class="footnote-marker">179</sup><i class="footnote">His oath formula, cursing himself if his statement should be found false. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 17a" href="/Shabbat.17a">Babli <i>Šabbat</i> 17a</a>.</i> if I did not see Simeon, my mother’s brother, lame in one of his legs, standing in the Temple court with his trumpet in his hand and blowing! Rebbi Aqiba answered him, maybe you saw him only at the time of assembly<sup class="footnote-marker">180</sup><i class="footnote">The command to call all the community in the desert by the sound of trumpets (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:3" href="/Numbers.10.3"><i>Num.</i> 10:3</a>) is extended to use trumpets to introduce the public Torah reading in the Temple at Tabernacles in the Sabbatical Year (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 31:10-13" href="/Deuteronomy.31.10-13"><i>Deut</i>. 31:10–13</a>).</i>; but I was saying, at the time of sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">181</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:10" href="/Numbers.10.10"><i>Num</i>. 10:10</a>; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sanhedrin 3:9:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sanhedrin.3.9.4"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 3:3 Note 155</a>.</i>. Rebbi Tarphon said to him, I would hit my sons but you did not deviate right or left. I am the one who heard but I could not explain. You derive it and agree with tradition. Therefore, anybody who separates from you is as if he separated himself from his life<sup class="footnote-marker">182</sup><i class="footnote">A similar text in <i>Sifry Num</i>. 75 (a better text <i>Yalqut</i> 725).</i>.
<i>The priest shall atone who was anointed</i><sup class="footnote-marker">183</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 16:32" href="/Leviticus.16.32"><i>Lev</i>. 16:32</a>. The problem is the legitimacy of a priest appointed <i>ad hoc</i> as High Priest to conduct the service of the Day of Atonement for which common priests are disqualified.</i>. Since the entire chapter is said about Aaron, from where [to include another priest? The verse says, <i>who was anointed</i>;]<sup class="footnote-marker">184</sup><i class="footnote">From B and the parallels in <i>Yoma</i> (<b>ו</b>) and <i>Megillah</i> (<b>מ</b>) (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Horayot 3:2:33" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Horayot.3.2.33">Note 170</a>). The first 30 verses of the Chapter mention Aaron exclusively.</i> not only the anointed with the anointing oil; from where the one clothed in multiple garb? The verse says, <i>who was inducted into office</i>. And from where another who was appointed<sup class="footnote-marker">185</sup><i class="footnote">In an emergency of the Day of Atonement where no formal session of a court can be held. Even when anointing oils was available, simple investiture ws enough.</i>? The verse says, <i>the priest shall atone</i><sup class="footnote-marker">186</sup><i class="footnote">Since it does not stress “the High Priest”, it follows that any priest can be appointed to fill the office.</i>. How is he being appointed? The rabbis of Caesarea in the name of Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Joseph, by mouth<sup class="footnote-marker">187</sup><i class="footnote">It does not need the laying on of hands nor a document of appointment. (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosafot on Yoma 12b" href="/Tosafot_on_Yoma.12b">Tosaphot <i>Yoma</i> 12b <i>s</i>,<i>v</i>. כהן</a>).</i>. Rebbi Zeˋira said, this implies that one may ordain Elders by word of mouth. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Ada said, a Mishnah says so: “Recant the four things that you are used to say and we shall make you president of the Court for Israel.<sup class="footnote-marker">188</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Eduyot 5:6" href="/Mishnah_Eduyot.5.6">Mishnah <i>Idiut</i> 5:6</a>. The oral promise was irrevocable.<br>Here end the parallels in <i>Yoma</i> and <i>Megillah</i>.</i>”
“Both are equal in the office of the day of Atonement,” etc.]<sup class="footnote-marker">189</sup><i class="footnote">The beginning of the discussion of Mishnah 5 is noted only in B.</i> <sup class="footnote-marker">190</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Sifra, Emor" href="/Sifra,_Emor"><i>Sifra Emor Parašah</i> 2(7</a>), on <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:13" href="/Leviticus.21.13"><i>Lev</i>. 21:13</a>. Since the High Priest was mentioned in the preceding verses, the pronoun is unnecessary by the rules of grammar. It is added for emphasis; only the High Priest is restricted to marrying a virgin.</i><i>He</i>, not the king. <i>He</i>, not the chieftain<sup class="footnote-marker">191</sup><i class="footnote">Since the king was mentioned separately, נָשִׂיא here cannot be identified as the king; it must be a tribal chieftain.</i>. <i>He</i>, to include the priest Anointed for War<sup class="footnote-marker">192</sup><i class="footnote">Since the rules of the High Priest were tied in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:10" href="/Leviticus.21.10"><i>Lev</i>. 21:10</a> to wearing the High Priest’s garments and the Anointed for War is required to wear these when asking the oracle, he is bound by all rules enumerated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:10-15" href="/Leviticus.21.10-15">vv. 10–15</a>.</i>. <i>A woman in her virginity he shall marry</i>; this excludes an adult whose hymen has atrophied. Rebbi Eleazar and Rebbi Simeon qualify the adult<sup class="footnote-marker">193</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:14" href="/Leviticus.21.14"><i>Lev</i>. 21:14</a>. The parallels in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 59a" href="/Yevamot.59a">Babli, <i>Yebamot</i> 59a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ketubot 97b" href="/Ketubot.97b"><i>Ketubot</i> 97b</a>, identify the first opinion as R. Meïr’s. It is agreed that if a girl is fully grown, the breaking of her hymen may not be noticed by the man.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">194</sup><i class="footnote">The interpretation of this paragraph depends on whether one considers the texts of L and B as two different texts or that the correct text is that of B, except for the name tradition identical with <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Terumot 8:1:6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Terumot.8.1.6"><i>Terumot</i> 8:2, Notes 29–31</a>, with the text of L badly corrupted. Since in the characterization of the sacrifice, the text of L is certainly corrupt, the second alternative has much to commend itself. In the text itself, the crucial point is whether to read אחר as אַחֵר “another” or אַחַר “after”. Since the text of L, but not that of B, refers to the High Priest, in the absence of a clear solution both texts are presented and explained.<br>In the text of L one refers to the statement in the Mishnah that an acting High Priest and a deposed one are equal in all but the service of the Day of Atonement. The question is whether the acting High Priest may take the required fist full of incense and the deposed one then may bring the incense to the inner altar and burn it there; or the acting High Priest receive the blood of his sacrifices and the deposed one sprinkle of the blood on the walls of the altar. The question is not asked anywhere else and the positive answer is difficult to accept. Therefore, it is better to accept the text of B, even though it does not refer to the High Priest, as necessary introduction to the following paragraph which does.<br>That text reads:<br>Rebbi Isaac asked, does this apply to the remaining actions? He took the fist full and afterwards burned it; he received and afterwards threw it, he burned and afterwards sprinkled? Rebbi Jacob bar Idi in the name of Rebbi Isaac: They made it like a robbed purification sacrifice which was not publicly known. This implies that if he took the fistful afterwards he burns it, if he received [the blood] afterwards he throws [it on the walls of the altar], he burned [the red cow] he afterwards sprinkles [water with its ashes to purify others].<br>As explained in <i>Terumot</i>, the question is asked about a Cohen who is informed that he is disbarred from the priesthood because of his birth from a woman forbidden to priests when he had completed one sacral action which by necessity must be followed by a different one. The answer is that the desecrated son of a Cohen who innocently started officiating may officiate to the end even though in the future he will be barred from officiating.</i> Rebbi Isaac asked, are these things so in all other things? He takes the fist full and the other burns it; he receives and the other throws, he burns and the other sprinkles? Rebbi Jacob bar Idi in the name of Rebbi Isaac: They made it like a (great) [robbed]<sup class="footnote-marker">195</sup><i class="footnote">The reference is to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Gittin 5:6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Gittin.5.6.1">Mishnah <i>Gittin</i> 5:5</a>, as explained in <i>Terumot</i>. The text of L is in parentheses, the correct text in brackets is from B. The point of the argument is missing here in both texts, that the purification offering is acceptable (i., e., that the Temple authorities are prohibited from inquiring into the way the offerer acquired his animal.)</i> purification sacrifice which was not publicly known. This implies that he takes the fistful and the other burns it, he receives and the other throws, he burns and the other sprinkles. <sup class="footnote-marker">196</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Terumot 8:1:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Terumot.8.1.7"><i>Terumot</i> 8:2, Notes 32–33</a>,40. If the High Priest after his elevation was found to be desecrated by his birth and thereby is removed, is this considered to be his death as far as the Sanctuary is concerned and releases any homicide sentenced during his tenure of office from the city of refuge or is his tenure as High Priest erased from the annals of the Sanctuary (<i>Makkot</i> 2:10–11)? No answer is given here; the first eventuality is chosen in <i>Terumot</i>.</i>Rebbi Berekhiah, Rebbi Jacob bar Idi: Rebbi Isaac asked. If he was standing sacrificing on the altar when it became known that he was the son of a divorcee or the son of a woman having received <i>ḥaliṣah</i>, how do you treat him? [As if]<sup class="footnote-marker">197</sup><i class="footnote">Text of B.</i> he had died and the homicide might return to his home town or should he be treated as one whose trial had been concluded without a High Priest and he never can leave from there?

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The High Priest rends his garment below, the common priest above<sup class="footnote-marker">198</sup><i class="footnote">Rending one’s garment is a required mourning rite for a close relative (as defined in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:2-3" href="/Leviticus.21.2-3"><i>Lev</i>. 21:2–3</a>). The High Priest is forbidden any mourning rites, including rending his garment (Mishnah 5). One allows him to make a tear at the bottom of his robe where nobody will notice it.</i>. The High Priest sacrifices while in deep mourning but does not eat; the common priest neither sacrifices nor eats<sup class="footnote-marker">199</sup><i class="footnote">“Deep mourning” is the time between the death of a close relative and his burial (on the same day or the following night). Since the High Priest is forbidden to leave the Sanctuary (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:12" href="/Leviticus.21.12"><i>Lev</i>. 21:12</a>) he must be permitted to officiate. But eating <i>sancta</i> while in deep mourning is forbidden to everybody (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 26:14" href="/Deuteronomy.26.14"><i>Deut</i>. 26:14</a>), including the High Priest (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 10:19-20" href="/Leviticus.10.19-20"><i>Lev</i>. 10:19–20</a>). The common priest is required to defile himself for the burial of a close relative (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:1-2" href="/Leviticus.21.1-2"><i>Lev</i>. 21:1–2</a>); automatically he is excluded from the Sanctuary and all its service.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">200</sup><i class="footnote">The entire Halakhah is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sanhedrin 3:4:2-5:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sanhedrin.3.4.2-5.4"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 3:1, Notes 33–56</a>.</i> Rebbi Eleazar in the name of Cahana: On top, high starting with the seam, below, low starting with the seam. Rebbi Joḥanan said, really low. Rebbi Joḥanan was going up to visit Rebbi Ḥanina; on the road he heard that he had died. He sent, brought his good Sabbath garment, and tore it. Rebbi Joḥanan disagrees with Rebbi Jehudah in two things, but Rebbi Eleazar in the name of Cahana follows Rebbi Jehudah. If following Rebbi Jehudah, he should not tear at all! This refers only to his father or mother, following Rebbi Meïr, as it was stated: One tears the seam for nobody who died except for father and mother, the words of Rebbi Meïr. Rebbi Jehudah says, any tear which does not completely sever the seam is a frivolous tear. How is that? It is said<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote">This is a simple copyist’s error for חוֹמֶר “a stringency”.</i> for the High Priest that he shall sever the seam completely.
“The High Priest sacrifices while in deep sorrow but does not eat, the words of Rebbi Meïr; Rebbi Jehudah says, the entire day. Rebbi Simeon says, he completely finishes the service he is engaged in and then leaves.” Between Rebbi Meïr and Rebbi Simeon there is one [difference], between Rebbi Jehudah and Rebbi Simeon there is one [difference]. Between Rebbi Meïr and Rebbi Jehudah is entering. Rebbi Jacob ben Dositheos: interruption is between them. Rebbi Meïr says, if he was inside, he leaves; if he was outside, he does not enter. Rebbi Jehudah says, if he was inside, he (leaves); if he was outside, he does not enter. Rebbi Simeon says, he completely finishes the service he is engaged in and then leaves. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rav Huna: a <i>baraita</i> is from Rebbi Simeon: “<i>The Sanctuary he shall not leave</i>, he may not leave with them, but he may leave after them. (But they enter and he leaves). If they are unseen he can be seen; he leaves with them up to the city gate, the words of Rebbi Meïr; Rebbi Jehudah said, he does not leave the Temple since it is said: <i>The Sanctuary he shall not leave</i>. If he left, he may not return.”
Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Eleazar: “Deep sorrow” is only for the dead, for it is written: <i>Its gates are in deep sorrow and mourning</i>. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Ada objected: Is it not written<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">Since the original statement of R. Simeon ben Laqish referred to a case where he is more restrictive than R. Joḥanan, it is inadmissible to quote him in support of a more lenient position. In the case considered there is unanimity that for a transgression committed as a commoner, which could not have been atoned for while one was elevated, the original obligation of a purification sacrifice of a female sheep or goat is re-instituted.</i>: <i>the fishermen are in deep sorrow</i>,<i>mourning are all who throw a fish-hook into the Nile</i>? Rebbi Ḥanina said, so is the <i>baraita</i>: there is no deep sorrow in impurity except for the dead. It was stated: “What is deep sorrow? From the moment of death until the moment of burial, the word of Rebbi. But the Sages say, the entire day.” It turns out that one describes leniencies and stringencies following Rebbi, leniencies and stringencies following the rabbis. What is the difference between them? If someone died and was buried within the hour. Following the rabbis, he is forbidden the entire day; following Rebbi he is forbidden only that hour. If the person died and was buried after three days. Following the rabbis, he is forbidden the entire day; following Rebbi he is forbidden up to three days. There came Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan, and Rav Ḥisda, both of whom said that Rebbi agrees with the Sages that he is forbidden only during the first day, as it was stated: Rebbi said, you know that deep mourning in the night is not biblical, since they said, “the deep mourner immerses himself and eats his Passover sacrifice in the evening.” But they said, deep mourning during daytime is biblical. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rebbi Huna: Explain it that the person was buried close to sundown and one cannot infer anything.

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Anything which is more frequent than another precedes the other<sup class="footnote-marker">203</sup><i class="footnote">Anything which is done more frequently is executed before anything less frequent is done. The statement of the Mishnah is repeated in <i>Zebahim</i> 10:1, where the implications for the Temple service are detailed. For example, if New Year’s Day falls on a Sabbath, the first sacrifices are the daily offerings (offered 365 days a year), followed by the Sabbath sacrifice (52 times), then the New Moon sacrifice (12 times), and last the New Year’s Day sacrifice (1). Synagogue practice imitates this rule.</i>. Anything more holy than another precedes the other<sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote">For example, if a person brings animals for a purification sacrifice, an elevation sacrifice, and a well-being sacrifice to the Temple, they have to be offered in this order (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Zevachim 10:2" href="/Mishnah_Zevachim.10.2">Mishnah <i>Zebahim</i> 10:2</a>).</i>. If the bull of the Anointed and the bull of the community are standing, the Anointed’s bull precedes the community’s bull in all its ceremonies<sup class="footnote-marker">205</sup><i class="footnote">The rules for the Court’s (the community’s) purification sacrifice (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 4:13-21" href="/Leviticus.4.13-21"><i>Lev</i>. 4:13–21</a>) are dependent on the Anointed’s sacrifice (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 4:1-12" href="/Leviticus.4.1-12"><i>Lev</i>. 4:1–12</a>). If they are offered simultaneously then the Anointed’s has precedence.</i>.<br>The man precedes the woman to be kept alive<sup class="footnote-marker">206</sup><i class="footnote">This usually is interpreted to mean that if a man and a woman are simultaneously in mortal danger, the man has to be saved first. But it also could mean that if a man and a woman are looking for a livelihood, the man has to be considered first.</i> and to regain his lost property<sup class="footnote-marker">207</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. Mishnah <i>Bava Mesiaˋ</i> 2:13.</i>. But the woman precedes the man for clothing<sup class="footnote-marker">208</sup><i class="footnote">A poor man will not be hurt by appearing in rags. A woman cannot possibly be seen in rags.</i> and to be freed from captivity<sup class="footnote-marker">209</sup><i class="footnote">A woman is more likely to be raped in captivity than a man.</i>. At a time when both are used for immorality<sup class="footnote-marker">210</sup><i class="footnote">If they are forced into prostitution, the man is in addition forced into homosexuality.</i>, the man precedes the woman.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “Anything which is more frequent than another,” etc. [“If the bull of the Anointed and the bull of the community are standing, the Anointed’s bull precedes the community’s bull”,]<sup class="footnote-marker">215</sup><i class="footnote">From B; a necessary introduction to the following text.</i> for one is atoning, the other is being atoned for<sup class="footnote-marker">216</sup><i class="footnote">This also is the reason given in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 13a" href="/Horayot.13a">Babli (13a</a>) for the precedence of a purification offering over a simultaneously presented elevation offering, both being most holy sacrifices.</i>. It is preferable that the atoner precede the atoned for, as it is written, <i>he shall atone for himself, and for his house</i>, <i>and for all the congregation of Israel</i><sup class="footnote-marker">217</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 16:17" href="/Leviticus.16.17"><i>Lev</i>. 16:17</a>. The argument really refers to the service of the Day of Atonement in its entirety, where the High Priest performs three acts of atonement, the first for himself and his family, the second for himself and the priests, and then the third for himself, the priests, and all of Israel. The priest performing the rite of atonement has to be purified himself before being able to serve others. (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Horayot 2:4" href="/Tosefta_Horayot.2.4">Tosephta <i>Horaiot</i> 2:4</a>, <i>Zevahim</i> 10:1).</i>. Between a voluntary gift of the Anointed and a voluntary gift of the prince, the voluntary gift of the Anointed has precedence<sup class="footnote-marker">218</sup><i class="footnote">Again because the priest has to act to present the king’s gift.</i>. Between a voluntary gift of the community and a voluntary gift of the prince, the voluntary gift of the prince has precedence<sup class="footnote-marker">219</sup><i class="footnote">Since he is the representative of the community.</i>. Between a voluntary gift of the Anointed and a voluntary gift of the community, which one has precedence? Let us hear from the following: A voluntary gift of the Anointed and rams of idolatry<sup class="footnote-marker">220</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. Chapter 1, Notes 122,135. For the number of rams, cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Horayot 1:6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Horayot.1.6.1">Mishnah 1:6</a>.</i> were standing. The rams of idolatry have precedence since their blood enters inside<sup class="footnote-marker">221</sup><i class="footnote">While this is not indicated elsewhere, if the bull is identified as the bull prescribed in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 4" href="/Leviticus.4"><i>Lev</i>. 4</a>, the ram is attached to a sacrifice whose blood is brought inside the Sanctuary and which, therefore, has precedence as the more holy sacrifice.</i>. He only said “since their blood enters inside;” this implies that between a voluntary gift of the Anointed and a voluntary gift of the community, the voluntary gift of the Anointed has precedence. If there were standing the bull of idolatry, the ram which accompanies it, and another purification sacrifice. The bull precedes the ram<sup class="footnote-marker">222</sup><i class="footnote">As will be explained later in this paragraph.</i>, the ram precedes the other purification sacrifice, and the other purification sacrifice precedes the bull<sup class="footnote-marker">223</sup><i class="footnote">The bull of idolatry is defined as an elevation sacrifice which takes second place after a purification sacrifice (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Horayot 3:4:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Horayot.3.4.2">Note 216</a>). The rules lead to an infinite loop.</i>. How is this done? Rebbi Yose said, since the ram is dependent in time on the bull, it is as if the bull preceded it, and the other purification sacrifice precedes the bull. The bull of idolatry precedes the ram because it precedes in Scripture<sup class="footnote-marker">224</sup><i class="footnote">The bull is prescribed in the first half of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:24" href="/Numbers.15.24"><i>Num</i>. 15:24</a>, the ram in the second half.</i>. Rebbi Samuel the brother of Rebbi Berekhiah asked: But then that of the New Moon should precede the ram which comes with it because it precedes [in Scripture.<sup class="footnote-marker">225</sup><i class="footnote">The sacrifices for the Day of the New Moon are prescribed in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 28:11" href="/Numbers.28.11"><i>Num</i>. 28:11</a> (elevation sacrifices) and 28:15 (the purification sacrifice). This contradicts our rule from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Horayot 3:4:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Horayot.3.4.2">Note 216</a>.</i>]<sup class="footnote-marker">226</sup><i class="footnote">Added from B, not absolutely necessary.</i> Rebbi Abba Mari said, you cannot do this; its <i>purification sacrifice</i> is defective<sup class="footnote-marker">227</sup><i class="footnote">The argument is very elliptic. The ram of idolatry follows the bull not really because it is mentioned later in the verse, but mainly because it is spelled defective, not as חטאת but only as חטת (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 13a" href="/Horayot.13a">Babli 13a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 90b" href="/Zevachim.90b"><i>Zevaḥim</i> 90b</a>). But the purification offering of the special days is directly connected with the daily offerings which start the day in the sanctuary (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 28:15" href="/Numbers.28.15"><i>Num</i>. 28:15</a>.)</i>: <i>After the permanent elevation offering it shall be made</i>, <i>with its libation</i>; it made it lean on the permanent elevation offering. Between the sacrifice of a man and the sacrifice of a woman, the man’s sacrifice has precedence<sup class="footnote-marker">228</sup><i class="footnote">If both are voluntary offerings of equal value. But an obligatory offering always has precedence over a voluntary one (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Zevachim 10:2" href="/Tosefta_Zevachim.10.2"><i>Tosephta</i> Zevaḥim 10:4</a>).</i>. That is, if both were equal. But if one was a bull and the other a lamb, it is what Rebbi Phineas said in the name of Rebbi Hoshaia: A slave brings a bull and his master brings a bull, the slave’s precedes the master’s, as we have stated there: “If the bull of the Anointed and the bull of the community are standing, the Anointed’s bull precedes the community’s bull in all its ceremonies.<sup class="footnote-marker">229</sup><i class="footnote">The argument is a <i>non sequitur</i>. Some commentators want to emend the text, in that the slave brings a bull but his master a goat. While this connects to the preceding, it severs the connection to the statement of R. Phineas. As a matter of principle, an emendation is totally inadmissible since the text is confirmed not only by the two independent sources here but also by <a class="refLink" data-ref="Vayikra Rabbah 5:4" href="/Vayikra_Rabbah.5.4"><i>Lev</i>. <i>Rabba</i> 5(4</a>) where the case of slave and master both bringing a bull follows a story about the merit of contributing to the support of scholars. As the text is presented here, one wonders why the following stories are placed here and what connection they could have with the topic of the Mishnah. But <i>Lev</i>. <i>Rabba</i>, an old text, shows that the case of slave and master is not a legal but a homiletic statement. There the argument is that the High Priest is the servant of the people; the Sanctuary is run only on behalf of the people. After the destruction of the Temple, the rabbinic establishment became the servant of the people, looking after their needs. Therefore, the rules of preference should be transferred from Temple service to the rabbinic establishment.</i>”
<sup class="footnote-marker">230</sup><i class="footnote">These texts are also in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Vayikra Rabbah 5:4" href="/Vayikra_Rabbah.5.4"><i>Lev</i>. <i>rabba</i> 5(4</a>); the first one only also in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Devarim Rabbah 4:8" href="/Devarim_Rabbah.4.8"><i>Deut</i>. <i>rabba</i>4(8</a>). Here also starts a Genizah fragment of half-lines (G) edited by L. Ginzberg (<i>Yerushalmi Fragments from the Genizah</i>, New York 1909, pp. 281–286.)</i> It happened that Rebbi Eliezer, Rebbi Joshua, and Rebbi Aqiba went to the dunes of Antiochia on the occasion of fundraising for the rabbis<sup class="footnote-marker">231</sup><i class="footnote">Projecting third and fourth Cent. fundraising into a story dated at the first. It is a typically oriental story where people do not get rich by commercial success but by finding a treasure.</i>. There was there a certain Abba Jehudah who gave alms generously. Once he lost his property, he saw our teachers and gave up hope about them. He went home looking sickly. His wife asked him, why are you looking sickly? He told her, our teachers are here and I do not know what I could do. His wife, who was even more pious than he, told him: You have a field left; go, sell half of it, and give to them. He went and did so, came to our teachers and gave them. Our teachers prayed for him and said to him, Abba Jehudah, the Holy One, praise to Him, may fill your want. After they left, he went to plough his half of the field. When he was ploughing in his half of the field, his cow sank down and broke [its leg]<sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote">Added from B.</i>. He went to lift her up when the Holy One, praise to Him, enlightened his eyes and he found a treasure. He said, my cow’s leg broke for my benefit. When our teachers returned, they inquired about him. They asked, how is Abba Jehudah doing? They answered, who can appear before Abba Jehudah? Abba Jehudah of his cattle, Abba Jehudah of his camels, Abba Jehudah of his donkeys! Abba Jehudah had returned to his former self; he came to our teachers to greet them. They asked him, how is Abba Jehudah doing? He told them, your prayer brought result and compound results. They told him, even though others had given more than you the last time, we wrote you on top of the honor list<sup class="footnote-marker">233</sup><i class="footnote">Greek τῖμος, an old poetic form of τιμή “esteem, value, honor” appearing also in late prose texts. The talmudic form supports late classical Greek lexicography; cf. also E. and H. Guggenheimer, <i>Talmudic Evidence for Greek Spelling</i>, Studi Classici in Onore di Quintino Cataudela, vol. 4, Catania 1972, pp. 71–72.ˋ</i>. They took him, made him sit with them, and recited for him this verse<sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 18:16" href="/Proverbs.18.16"><i>Prov</i>. 18:16</a>.</i>: <i>The gifts of a man put him at ease</i>; <i>in front of great ones they will make him rest.</i>
Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba held a pledging for a certain house of study at Tiberias. There was one there of the family of Bar Silene, who pledged a pound of gold. (The Elder Rebbi Ḥiyya) [Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba]<sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote">The impossible text in parentheses is from L; the correct text in brackets is from B.</i> took him, made him sit with him, and recited for him this verse: <i>The gifts of a man put him at ease</i>, etc.
<sup class="footnote-marker">236</sup><i class="footnote">In B, the last two paragraphs are in the inverse order. This is the chronologically correct order, teacher followed by student. Chronological consistency is one of the hallmarks of the Babli.</i> Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish went up to Bostra. Over there was a cheater. God forbid that he was a cheater, but he cheated in charity. He looked how much the community pledged, and he pledged the same amount<sup class="footnote-marker">237</sup><i class="footnote">His cheating was that he gave the minimum amount necessary to maintain his standing as the richest man around.</i>. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish took him, made him sit with him, and recited for him this verse: <i>The gifts of a man put him at ease</i>, etc.
“The man precedes the woman,” etc. So far if each one was to be kept alive or each one was for clothing. If one was to be kept alive and the other for clothing<sup class="footnote-marker">238</sup><i class="footnote">The question really is raised about the livelihood of a woman and the clothing of a man.</i>? Let us hear from the following, as Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said in the name of Rebbi [Ḥanina ben]<sup class="footnote-marker">239</sup><i class="footnote">From B; no R. Antigonos is known from other sources. G is defective here but the length of the lacuna supports the reading of B.</i> Antigonos, the clothing of the wife of a fellow<sup class="footnote-marker">240</sup><i class="footnote">Here “fellow” and “vulgar” are the technical terms defined in the Introduction to Tractate Demai, respectively of a person strictly keeping all rules of levitic purity (long after the destruction of the Temple) and tithes, and one disregarding the rules of purity and lax in the observance of the rules of tithes.</i> and the life of a vulgar; the clothing of the wife of a fellow has precedence over the life of a vulgar because of the dignity of the fellow. He only said that the clothing of the wife of a fellow was like the life of the fellow<sup class="footnote-marker">241</sup><i class="footnote">B has a different text: “He only said between the clothing of the wife of a fellow and the livelihood of a vulgar.” The best is the reading of G: “The clothing of the wife of a fellow during the lifetime of the fellow.”</i>. But if there was one to be kept alive and one for clothing, the one to be kept alive has precedence.
“Between his lost property and his father’s lost property, his own has precedence. Between his lost property and his teacher’s lost property, his own has precedence. Between his father’s lost property and his teacher’s lost property, his teacher’s lost property has precedence, for his father brought him to the life of this world, but his teacher who taught him wisdom brought him to the life of the future world.<sup class="footnote-marker">243</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Bava Mesiˋa</i> 2:13, Note 135.</i>” The teacher who taught him (Mishnah) [wisdom]<sup class="footnote-marker">244</sup><i class="footnote">The text in parentheses is from L, the one in brackets from B. The text of B is the one from the Mishnah, the one of L can be justified as text of the Tanna R. Yose in the following paragraph.</i>, not the teacher who taught him Scripture. “But if his father was his teacher’s equal, his father’s lost property has precedence.”
What does it help<sup class="footnote-marker">245</sup><i class="footnote">How does the fact that his father was as learned as his teacher change the argument of the Mishnah?</i>? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, if half of his learning was from one and half of his learning from the other. His father’s lost property if half of his learning was from him and his mother’s lost property if she was divorced from his father, which has precedence<sup class="footnote-marker">246</sup><i class="footnote">As long as his mother was married to his father, his father has precedence since his wife also is bound to honor him (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Keritot 6:9" href="/Mishnah_Keritot.6.9">Mishnah <i>Keritut</i> 6:9</a>). But the divorced mother in all respects is equal to the father (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 31a" href="/Kiddushin.31a">Babli <i>Qiddušin</i> 31a</a>). If the father was also the teacher then he had precedence as teacher. But if he was only a partial teacher, is his claim strong enough or does the son still have the choice whom to help first?</i>? Does his father’s have precedence or only if all his learning was from him? His teacher’s lost property if half of his learning was from him and his mother’s lost property if she was divorced from his father, which has precedence<sup class="footnote-marker">248</sup><i class="footnote">Is the teacher who taught him half his learning the teacher in the sense of the Mishnah or not?</i>? Does his teacher’s have precedence or only if all his learning was from him? His lost property, and his father’s lost property, and his mother’s lost property, and his teacher’s lost property. His own precedes his father’s, his father’s his mother’s, and his mother’s his teacher’s. Is that not a Mishnah, “the man precedes the woman to be kept alive and to return his lost property”? They wanted to say, if his teacher was not there<sup class="footnote-marker">249</sup><i class="footnote">The language implies that the statements in question are tannaitic, similar to the first part of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Horayot 2:5-6" href="/Tosefta_Horayot.2.5-6">Tosephta <i>Horaiot</i> 2:5</a>.</i>. He comes to tell you, even if his teacher was there. He, and his mother, and his teacher, and his father, were in captivity. He precedes his mother, his mother his teacher, and his teacher his father<sup class="footnote-marker">250</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 13a" href="/Horayot.13a">Babli 13a</a>.</i>. Is that not a Mishnah, “but the woman precedes the man for clothing and to be freed from captivity”? They wanted to say, if his teacher was not there. He comes to tell you, even if his teacher was there.
<sup class="footnote-marker">251</sup><i class="footnote">For the following, cf. <i>Bava mesiaˋ</i> 3:13, Notes 136–145; <i>Moˋed qatan</i> 3:7.</i> Who is the teacher who taught him wisdom? The one who taught him first, the words of Rebbi Meïr. Rebbi Jehudah said, the one from whom he received most of his instruction. Rebbi Yose said, anyone who explained a Mishnah to him.<sup class="footnote-marker">252</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Horayot 2:5-6" href="/Tosefta_Horayot.2.5-6">Tosephta 2:5</a>, <i>Bava mesiaˋ</i> 2:30.</i>” Rebbi Abbahu came in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: Practice follows him who said, the one from whom he received most of his instruction. Why did he not explain that this follows Rebbi Jehudah? There are Tannaïm who state it switched<sup class="footnote-marker">253</sup><i class="footnote">The name tradition in the Tosephta is not certain.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar tore his garment for his first teacher. Samuel took off [his phylacteries] for one who had explained a Mishnah to him<sup class="footnote-marker">254</sup><i class="footnote">As a sign of mourning. The phylacteries are identified as the “splendor” which Ezechiel had to remove in mourning, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 24:17" href="/Ezekiel.24.17"><i>Ez</i>. 24:17</a>. The text in <i>Bava mesiaˋ</i> parallels the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bava Metzia 33a" href="/Bava_Metzia.33a">Babli (<i>Bava mesiaˋ</i> 33a</a>) in reporting that he tore his garment.</i>. What Mishnah did he explain to him? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, “for one key he has to go down to his arm-pit and one opens straight.<sup class="footnote-marker">255</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Tamid 3:6" href="/Mishnah_Tamid.3.6">Mishnah <i>Tamid</i> 3:6</a>.</i>” What means “for one he has to gown to his arm-pit,” he had to lower his hand under his arm-pit until it could be opened<sup class="footnote-marker">256</sup><i class="footnote">The doors of the Temple Hall could be opened only from the inside. When the door was locked, a Cohen entered from a small side door which led to a guard room. The lock of this side door was hidden; the Cohen had to take the key, lower his entire arm to the arm-pit behind the partition wall and only then could insert the key. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tamid 30b" href="/Tamid.30b"><i>Tamid</i> 30b</a>.</i>. Rebbi Ḥanania<sup class="footnote-marker">257</sup><i class="footnote">With G read “Hanina”.</i> was leaning on Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba in Sepphoris, when he saw everybody running. He asked him, why is everybody running? He answered, Rebbi Joḥanan is sitting preaching in Rebbi Banaia’s house of study and everybody is running to hear him. He said, praised be the Merciful Who showed me fruits while I am alive. In <i>Agadah</i> I explained him everything except Proverbs and Ecclesiastes<sup class="footnote-marker">258</sup><i class="footnote">This proves that even a teacher of homiletics has the rank of teacher.</i>.
“If both of them stand in [a house of] ill repute, the man precedes the woman.” Why? For a woman it is natural, for a man it is not natural<sup class="footnote-marker">210</sup><i class="footnote">If they are forced into prostitution, the man is in addition forced into homosexuality.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">259</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Horayot 2:5-6" href="/Tosefta_Horayot.2.5-6">Tosephta 2:5</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Horayot 2:6" href="/Tosefta_Horayot.2.6">6</a>; <i>Thr</i>. <i>rabbati</i> 4(4); <a class="refLink" data-ref="Gittin 58a" href="/Gittin.58a">Babli <i>Gittin</i> 58a</a>.</i> It happened that Rebbi Joshua went to Rome. They informed him about a child from Jerusalem who was reddish with beautiful eyes, good to look at, and his locks ordered in curls<sup class="footnote-marker">260</sup><i class="footnote">A combination of biblical adjectives, <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 17:42" href="/I_Samuel.17.42"><i>1S</i>. 17:42</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Song of Songs 5:11" href="/Song_of_Songs.5.11"><i>Cant</i>. 5:11</a>.</i>, standing in [a house of] ill repute. Rebbi Joshua went to check him out. When he came to the door, Rebbi Joshua started and said, <i>who gave Jacob to be booty and Israel to plunderers, is that not the Eternal</i><sup class="footnote-marker">261</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 42:24" href="/Isaiah.42.24"><i>Is</i>. 42:24</a>.</i>? The child answered him and told him, <i>it is because we sinned against Him; they did not want to walk in His ways and did not listen to His teaching</i><sup class="footnote-marker">261</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 42:24" href="/Isaiah.42.24"><i>Is</i>. 42:24</a>.</i>. Immediately his eyes were flowing with tears and he said, I take as my witnesses heaven and earth that I shall not move from here until I buy his freedom. He bought his freedom for much money, sent him to the Land of Israel, and quoted for him this verse, <i>the dear children of Zion</i><sup class="footnote-marker">262</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Lamentations 4:2" href="/Lamentations.4.2"><i>Thr</i>. 4:2</a>.</i> etc.

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> A priest precedes a Levite, a Levite an Israel, an Israel a bastard, a bastard a Gibeonite<sup class="footnote-marker">211</sup><i class="footnote">The bastard has (in general) genuinely Jewish parents; the Gibeonites became Jewish by deceit.</i>, a Gibeonite a proselyte<sup class="footnote-marker">212</sup><i class="footnote">The Gibeonite’s parents were Jewish, the proselyte’s not.</i>, a proselyte a manumitted slave. When? If they are all equal<sup class="footnote-marker">213</sup><i class="footnote">In religious learning.</i>. But if the bastard was learned and the High Priest ignorant, the learned bastard precedes<sup class="footnote-marker">214</sup><i class="footnote">In honor due to him.</i> the ignorant High Priest.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “A priest precedes a Levite, a Levite an Israel, an Israel a bastard,” etc. <sup class="footnote-marker">264</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Horayot 2:9" href="/Tosefta_Horayot.2.9">Tosephta 2:10</a>.</i>“A Sage has precedence over the king, the king has precedence over the High Priest, the High Priest has precedence over a prophet, a prophet has precedence over the Anointed for War, the Anointed for war has precedence over the head of the watch<sup class="footnote-marker">265</sup><i class="footnote">Of one of the 24 watches into which the Cohanim were organized (<a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 24" href="/I_Chronicles.24"><i>1Chr</i>. 24</a>), each of which served for one week in the Temple.</i>, the head of the watch has precedence over the [head of a] clan<sup class="footnote-marker">266</sup><i class="footnote">A clan of priests belonging to one of the watches. The correct reading here is that of G, confirmed later also by L (lines 61ff.)</i>, the [head of a] clan has precedence over the executive officer<sup class="footnote-marker">267</sup><i class="footnote">The permanent member of the Temple staff who organizes the daily routine. As a paid official he comes after the volunteers who do the actual officiating. In Babylonian sources, his title is spelled אמרכל.</i>, the executive officer has precedence over the treasurer<sup class="footnote-marker">268</sup><i class="footnote">The Temple treasurer.</i>, the treasurer has precedence over a common priest, a common priest has precedence over a Levite, a Levite over an Israel, an Israel over a bastard, a bastard over a Gibeonite, a Gibeonite over a proselyte, a proselyte over a manumitted slave. When? If they are all equal. But if the bastard was learned and the High Priest ignorant, the learned bastard precedes the ignorant High Priest.”
“A Sage has precedence over the king.” If a Sage dies, we do not have a replacement<sup class="footnote-marker">269</sup><i class="footnote">This restricts the statement to a truly outstanding Sage. In G, this is not a reference to the text of the Mishnah but a continuation of the statement that a learned bastard has precedence over the boorish High Priest, “and similarly, a Sage has precedence over a king.” The text of L is that of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Horayot 2:8" href="/Tosefta_Horayot.2.8">Tosephta 2:8</a>.</i>. If a king dies, all of Israel are qualified for the kingdom<sup class="footnote-marker">270</sup><i class="footnote">This legitimizes non-Davidic kings. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 13a" href="/Horayot.13a">Babli (13a</a>) agrees. The current printed Babli editions were adulterated by a censor who inserted “king of Israel”, to preserve the superiority of the ruler by the grace of God. Already Maimonides in his Commentary to the Mishnah notes that all the precedences enumerated in this Mishnah are ethical only, rather than practical.</i>.
Rebbi Joḥanan said, all these 40 days which Moses spent on the Mountain, he studied Torah and forgot it. At the end it was given to him as a gift. Why so much? To return the stupid ones<sup class="footnote-marker">271</sup><i class="footnote">To encourage people who do not understand a subject to return to study; they can always hope that at the end the understanding will be given to them in their sleep. The argument would be better if addressed to scientists who fail to solve a problem; if they persevere they have the hope to finally receive the answer from Heaven in their sleep.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">272</sup><i class="footnote">The homily here is a considerably shortened version of one in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 1:5:2-6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.1.5.2-6.1"><i>Berakhot</i> 1:8</a> (5c l. 29; Notes 322–324) where R. Illai (La) notes that 4 useful things mentioned in <i>Job</i> can be replaced when lost. Text B has the full quotes but still lacks the necessary introduction. The homily of R. Levi is unchanged.</i> When Rebbi Simeon ben Zevid died, Rebbi Illai rose and eulogized him. <i>But silver has a source</i><sup class="footnote-marker">213</sup><i class="footnote">In religious learning.</i>, etc. <i>Iron is taken from dust</i><sup class="footnote-marker">274</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 28:2" href="/Job.28.2"><i>Job</i> 28:2</a>.</i>, etc. Those, if they are lost, have replacement. But a scholar who died, who can bring us one similar to him? <i>Wisdom, where can it be found</i><sup class="footnote-marker">275</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 28:20" href="/Job.28.20"><i>Job</i> 28:20</a>.</i>, etc. <i>It is hidden from the eyes of all living</i><sup class="footnote-marker">276</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 28:21" href="/Job.28.21"><i>Job</i> 28:21</a>.</i>, etc. Rebbi Levi said, if the brothers of Joseph lost their spirit because they found a find, as it is written, <i>they lost their spirit</i><sup class="footnote-marker">277</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 42:28" href="/Genesis.42.28"><i>Gen.</i> 42:28</a>.</i>, we, who lost Rebbi Simeon bar Zevid, so much more<sup class="footnote-marker">278</sup><i class="footnote">Note in G the unusual form עַל אַחַת כַּמָּה וְאַחַת כַּמָּה for the common עַל אַחַת כַּמָּה וְכַמָּה “so much more”.</i>!
<sup class="footnote-marker">279</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Horayot 2:8" href="/Tosefta_Horayot.2.8">Tosephta 2:9</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 13a" href="/Horayot.13a">Babli 13a</a>.</i> The king has precedence over the High Priest, as it is written: <i>You shall let my son Solomon ride</i><sup class="footnote-marker">280</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 1:33" href="/I_Kings.1.33"><i>1K</i>. 1:33</a>.</i>, etc. The High Priest over the prophet, as it is written: <i>There</i>, <i>Ṣadoq the Priest and Nathan the Prophet shall anoint him as king</i><sup class="footnote-marker">281</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 1:34" href="/I_Kings.1.34"><i>1K</i>. 1:34</a>.</i>, etc. He mentioned Ṣadoq before Nathan. Rebbi Jonah in the name of Rebbi Ḥama bar Ḥanina: The prophet folds his hands and feet and sits before the High Priest<sup class="footnote-marker">282</sup><i class="footnote">He sits on the floor or the carpet with his feet folded under him.</i>. What is his reason? <i>Listen</i>, <i>Joshua the High Priest</i>, <i>you and your friends who are sitting before you</i><sup class="footnote-marker">283</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 3:8" href="/Zechariah.3.8"><i>Zach</i>. 3:8</a>.</i><i>.</i> I could think that they were common people; the verse says, <i>because they are men of miracle</i>, and “miracle” only means prophecy, as you say, <i>and he gave you a sign or a miracle</i><sup class="footnote-marker">284</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 13:2" href="/Deuteronomy.13.2"><i>Deut</i>. 13:2</a>.</i><i>.</i>
<sup class="footnote-marker">285</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Horayot 2:9" href="/Tosefta_Horayot.2.9">Tosephta 2:10</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 13a" href="/Horayot.13a">Babli 13a</a> (cf. Notes 264–268).</i>“A prophet has precedence over the Anointed for War, the Anointed for War has precedence over the head of the watch, the head of the watch has precedence over the head of a clan, the head of a clan has precedence over the executive officer, the executive officer has precedence over the treasurer, the treasurer has precedence over a common priest, a common priest has precedence over a Levite, a Levite over an Israel (an Israel over a bastard<sup class="footnote-marker">286</sup><i class="footnote">This clause was erased by the scribe of L, it is not in B or G.</i>).” Is not the Levite equal [to an Israel]<sup class="footnote-marker">287</sup><i class="footnote">Added from B and G; must be understood in L.</i>? Rebbi Abun said, this was taught in the days of the podium<sup class="footnote-marker">288</sup><i class="footnote">When the Levites had a role in Temple worship, either as singers on the podium or as watchmen. The statement that Levites are no different from Israel shows that the custom that Levites have to pour water of the Cohen’s hands before he goes to pronounce the priestly blessing is not talmudic. (The source is <i>Zohar</i> III, 146b; the custom is not followed by Yemenites and some other Oriental groups.)</i>. Rebbi Abun said, a proselyte and an apostate, the apostate has preference because of what had happened<sup class="footnote-marker">289</sup><i class="footnote">If a Gentile comes to a rabbi asking to become a proselyte and a Jewish apostate comes at the same time asking to be readmitted to the Jewish community, the rabbi has to deal with the apostate’s case first, not to turn him away permanently as in the case of Joshua ben Perahia (or Jehudah ben Tabbai) (<i>Sanhedrin</i> 6:6, Note 79) and similar stories about Elisha and Gehazi (<i>Sanhedrin</i> 10:3, Notes 284,286).</i>. “Why does everybody run after a proselyte woman, but not after a freedwoman? For the proselyte is presumed to have been guarding herself but the freedwoman<sup class="footnote-marker">290</sup><i class="footnote">As long as the freedwoman (Latin: <i>libertina</i>) was a slave, she could not marry and, therefore, was free to have guiltless sex with any man she pleased (except Jews.) She cannot be supposed to have changed her ways radically upon manumission. The proselyte as a free woman is supposed to be married as a virgin (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 13a" href="/Horayot.13a">Babli 13a</a>).</i> is presumed to be irresponsible.” And why does everybody (run after a rat)<sup class="footnote-marker">291</sup><i class="footnote">To kill them. This is the text of L, taken from the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 13a" href="/Horayot.13a">Babli 13a</a>, but it seems that one should accept the text of B and G in brackets.</i> [inquire after a slave]<sup class="footnote-marker">292</sup><i class="footnote">Since the slave has no <i>persona</i> in law, he is irresponsible, and cannot be sued for damages. Therefore, a prospective buyer is well advised to inquire whether this slave may in the future expose him to suits for damages caused by his slave.</i>? Because his dealings are bad for people. Rebbi Joḥanan said, do not believe a slave up to sixteen generations. <i>Ismael ben Netaniah ben Elishama of royal descent came and slew Gedaliahu at Miṣpah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">293</sup><i class="footnote">Here ends the fragment G.</i>.
Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said: A head<sup class="footnote-marker">294</sup><i class="footnote">The learned in the law, i. e., the rabbinic authorities.</i> and an Elder<sup class="footnote-marker">295</sup><i class="footnote">The tribal heads, paradigms for later political office holders.</i>, the (Elder) [head]<sup class="footnote-marker">296</sup><i class="footnote">The text in parentheses is that of L, the one in brackets that of B,G. The reason given shows that the latter text was intended by all sources.</i> has precedence, for nobody is a head if he is not an Elder. What is his reason? <i>All of you are standing today</i><sup class="footnote-marker">297</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 29:9" href="/Deuteronomy.29.9"><i>Deut</i>. 29:9</a>; later in the verse the tribal heads are mentioned before the Elders.</i>, etc. <i>Joshua assembled all Elders of Israel at Sichem</i><sup class="footnote-marker">298</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 24:1" href="/Joshua.24.1"><i>Jos</i>. 24:1</a> (misquoted); Elders are mentioned before tribal heads. Similarly in 23:2.</i>. Moses preferred heads over Elders; Joshua preferred Elders over heads. Moses preferred heads over Elders because all were his students. Joshua preferred Elders over heads because not all were his students. Moses preferred heads over Elders because he did not need them in conquering the Land; Joshua preferred Elders over heads because be needed them in conquering the Land<sup class="footnote-marker">299</sup><i class="footnote">While he did not need them for military decisions, they prepared the maps for the distribution of the Land (Chapter 18).</i>. Moses preferred heads over Elders because he needed no exertion in the study of Torah, Joshua preferred Elders over heads because he had to exert himself in the study of Torah. Rebbi Joshua of Sikhnin in the name of Rebbi Levi: Moses preferred heads over Elders because he saw by the Holy Ghost that in the future Israel will be (reasonable) [in trouble]<sup class="footnote-marker">293,</sup><i class="footnote">Here ends the fragment G.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">296</sup><i class="footnote">The text in parentheses is that of L, the one in brackets that of B,G. The reason given shows that the latter text was intended by all sources.</i> with governments and their heads will stand up for them<sup class="footnote-marker">300</sup><i class="footnote">A clear declaration of the priority of the political leadership over the religious.</i>.
It was stated: The systematizer has precedence over the dialectician<sup class="footnote-marker">302</sup><i class="footnote">The scholar who can bring order into the vast amount of rabbinic traditions is on a higher level than the one who finds apparent contradictions between traditional statements and explains them by finding the underlying principles. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 14a" href="/Horayot.14a">Babli (14a</a>) the question is between “Sinai” and “one who uproots mountains” (and grinds them down), i. e., between a living encyclopedia and a practitioner of dialectics, and it is reported that in Galilee Sinai was preferred. There is no mention there about an effort at systematizing and in fact it is in general impossible to derive a valid rule of practice by basing oneself on one talmudic discussion alone, but all Tractates of the Babli have simultaneously to be considered.</i>. Rebbi Samuel, Rebbi Berekhia’s brother, asked: Even like Rebbi Immi? He told him, what do you want from Rebbi Immi? He is a dialectician<sup class="footnote-marker">303</sup><i class="footnote">In B: “He is both a systematizer and a dialectician.” In both Talmudim, the teachings of R. Immi and his companion R. Yasa are too sporadic to allow a judgment between the two versions.</i>. This means, the Mishnah has precedence over Scripture<sup class="footnote-marker">304</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Mishnah is a first attempt at systematizing Jewish teaching, its study, while presupposing a prior study of Scripture, is on a higher level since it is less anecdotal or self-contradictory.</i>. The following supports this, as Rebbi Simeon ben Ioḥai stated, one who studies Scripture is a qualification which is not a qualification. But the rabbis consider Scripture equally with the Mishnah<sup class="footnote-marker">305</sup><i class="footnote">They agree to the value of analysis and explanation of Scripture also independent of traditional interpretations.</i>. Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman said, the Mishnah has precedence over the Talmud. What is the reason? <i>Acquire wisdom, acquire understanding</i><sup class="footnote-marker">306</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 4:5" href="/Proverbs.4.5"><i>Prov</i>. 4:5</a>. “Wisdom” is identified here as the Mishnah, the encyclopedia of traditional knowledge. “Understanding” is the explanation of the formulaic statements of the Mishnah, the Talmud, whether formulated in one of the Talmudim or in a prior state of oral explanation. Wisdom precedes understanding.</i>, etc. Rebbi Joḥanan said, the Talmud has precedence over the Mishnah. What is the reason? <i>Is acquiring wisdom not better than pure gold</i><sup class="footnote-marker">307</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 16:16" href="/Proverbs.16.16"><i>Prov</i>. 16:16</a>. The verse reads: <i>Is acquiring wisdom not better than pure gold, acquisition of understanding more select than silver</i>? Here also wisdom precedes understanding, but silver is everyday coin; gold is used only for major transactions and by the very rich.</i><i>?</i> How does Rebbi Joḥanan explain Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman’s reason? Water is cheap, wine is expensive. It is possible for the world to exist without wine; it is impossible for the world to exist without water<sup class="footnote-marker">308</sup><i class="footnote">In both verses, the less valuable but more essential is mentioned in second place. This does not make the second less essential.</i>. How does Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman explain Rebbi Joḥanan’s reason? Salt is cheap, pepper is expensive. It is possible for the world to exist without pepper; it is impossible for the world to exist without salt<sup class="footnote-marker">309</sup><i class="footnote">He agrees that without interpretation and explanation (“the Talmud”) the Mishnah cannot be applied; the salt of the Talmud, the silver, is absolutely necessary. This does not diminish the value of the gold.<br>A different version of the preceding arguments is in <i>Massekhet Sopherim</i> 15:7, 8.</i>. Always pursue the Mishnah more than the Talmud. That is, before Rebbi incorporated most Mishnaiot into it<sup class="footnote-marker">310</sup><i class="footnote">Here it is intimated that Rebbi’s edition of the Mishnah from the start was intended as providing the skeleton around which a systematic exposition of the Talmud, the oral tradition, could be organized. In this way, the Mishnah automatically is studied in a privileged way if the Talmud is studied. Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Vayikra Rabbah 21:4" href="/Vayikra_Rabbah.21.4"><i>Lev. rabba</i> 21(4</a>) which declares the study of the Mishnah as prerequisite for everything else.</i>. But since Rebbi incorporated most Mishnaiot into it, pursue the Talmud more than the Mishnah.
Rebbi Samuel, son of Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun<sup class="footnote-marker">311</sup><i class="footnote">One of the very last Amoraim mentioned in the Yerushalmi. He explains why his generation turned from work on a Talmud to work on Midrashim.</i>, preached: <i>A rich man is wise in his own eyes, but an understanding poor man will think little of him</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">312</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 28:11" href="/Proverbs.28.11"><i>Prov</i>. 28:11</a>. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kohelet Rabbah 6:2" href="/Kohelet_Rabbah.6.2"><i>Eccl. rabba</i> 6:2</a>, end.</i><i>A rich man is wise in his own eyes,</i> this is the master of Talmud. <i>But an understanding poor man will think little of him</i><sup class="footnote-marker">313</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. Arabic حقر “to despise somebody or something, think little of him.”</i>, that is the master of homiletics. A parable of two people who entered a city, in the hand of one are gold bars, in the other’s hand small change. The holder of the gold bars cannot spend them and survive; the holder of small change can spend it to survive<sup class="footnote-marker">314</sup><i class="footnote">Nobody comes to hear lectures on Talmud, everybody comes to hear a preacher. Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bava Batra 145b" href="/Bava_Batra.145b">Babli <i>Bava batra</i> 145b</a>. For a negative view of homiletics three generations earlier cf. <i>Maˋserot</i> 3:10 Note 161 (Sopherim Chapter 15).</i>.
Rebbi Aḥa preached: <i>Scales and balances of justice are the Eternal’s; His work are all stones in the purse</i><sup class="footnote-marker">315</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 16:11" href="/Proverbs.16.11"><i>Prov</i>. 16:11</a>. The purse is the container in which weight stones are kept (<i>Deut</i>. 25:13, <i>Mi</i>. 6:11). It may also mean the wallet where money is kept, <i>Prov</i>. 1:14, <i>Is</i>. 46:6. The sermon identifies the two and declares all religious studies of equal value.</i>. “Scales” is Scripture. “Balances” are the Mishnah. “Justice” is the Talmud. “The Eternal’s” are the additions<sup class="footnote-marker">316</sup><i class="footnote">The extra-talmudic texts; not only Tosephta collections but also Midrashim and similar compositions.</i>. <i>His work are all stones in the purse</i>; they all take their wages from the same purse.
<sup class="footnote-marker">317</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Kohelet Rabbah 6:2" href="/Kohelet_Rabbah.6.2"><i>Eccl. rabba</i> 6:2</a>.</i> Rebbi Abba bar Cahana went to a certain place where he found Rebbi Levi installed and preaching: <i>A man to whom God gives riches, and properties</i>, <i>and honor</i>,<i>and nothing is missing of anything he might desire</i>, <i>but</i> <i>God does not let him take possession to eat from it</i>, <i>for a stranger will eat from it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">318</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ecclesiastes 6:2" href="/Ecclesiastes.6.2"><i>Eccl.</i> 6:2</a>.</i>.<i>Riches</i>, that is Scripture. <i>Properties</i>, these are practices<sup class="footnote-marker">319</sup><i class="footnote">A code of practices in a culture of oral transmission was a very valuable property.</i>. <i>And honor</i>, these are the additions<sup class="footnote-marker">316</sup><i class="footnote">The extra-talmudic texts; not only Tosephta collections but also Midrashim and similar compositions.</i>. <i>And nothing is missing of anything he might desire</i>, these are the great Mishnah collections<sup class="footnote-marker">320</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Baraita</i> collections such as underlying the later Tosephta, or Mishnah collections preceding or competing with Rebbi’s Mishnah. <i>Eccl. rabba</i> adds R. Aqiba’s Mishnah.</i>, such as the Mishnah of Rebbi Ḥuna<sup class="footnote-marker">321</sup><i class="footnote">No collection of Rebbi Huna is known; also he would be an Amora of a later generation, unable to collect an independent collection. In <i>Eccl. rabba</i>, the reference is correctly to R. Hiyya (the Elder.)</i>, the Mishnah of Rebbi Hoshaia, or the Mishnah of Bar Qappara. <i>But God does not let him take possession to eat from it</i>, that is the master of Aggadah who neither prohibits nor permits, neither declares impure nor pure. <i>For a stranger will eat from it</i>, that is the master of Talmud<sup class="footnote-marker">322</sup><i class="footnote">Who has to master all the preceding topics and has the right to decide between forbidden and permitted acts.</i>. Rebbi Abba bar Cahana got up and kissed him on his head, saying, just as you were worthy to preach this standing, may you be worthy preaching this sitting<sup class="footnote-marker">323</sup><i class="footnote">R. Levi, who became the foremost preacher of his time, at this moment was rabbi of a small congregation who delivered his sermons in person standing in front of his congregation. R. Abba blessed him that he should become the head of a school who would deliver the concept of his speech to an Amora, a professional speaker, who would elaborate on the topics given to him by the head who remained seated.</i>.
If they intended to appoint Elders, from where do they appoint? From Tiberias or from the South<sup class="footnote-marker">324</sup><i class="footnote">The main Academy was at Tiberias in Galilee. There were minor centers of learning in the South, at Lydda and at Kefar Darom, in the plain which in Second Temple times was part of Judea. The question was which center of learning should be the first to propose candidates for ordination by the Patriarch.</i>? Rebbi Simon said, <i>Jehudah shall go first</i><sup class="footnote-marker">325</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Judges 1:2" href="/Judges.1.2"><i>Jud</i>. 1:2</a>. R. Simon came from the South.</i>. Rebbi Mana said to him, this refers to war. But for ordination, <i>those who see the face of the king, sitting first in government</i><sup class="footnote-marker">326</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Esther 1:14" href="/Esther.1.14"><i>Esther</i> 1:14</a>. The preeminent rabbis at this time were in Tiberias.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">327</sup><i class="footnote">The same text in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 9:15:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.9.15.7"><i>Sotah</i> 9:17 Note 265</a>; most of the story in greater detail <i>Sotah</i> 9:13–14, Notes 212–218, and the parallels given there in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Horayot 3:5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Horayot.3.5.1">Note 212</a>.</i> Rebbi Jacob bar Idi in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: It happened that the Elders assembled in the upper story of the House Gadya at Jericho when there came a disembodied voice and told them, there are two among you worthy of the Holy Spirit and one of them is Hillel the Elder. They looked at Samuel Minor. Then the Elders assembled in the upper story at Jabneh when there came a disembodied voice and told them, there are two among you worthy of the Holy Spirit and one of them is Samuel Minor. They looked at Eliezer ben Hyrcanos. They were happy that their opinion coincided with that of the Holy Spirit<sup class="footnote-marker">327</sup><i class="footnote">The same text in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 9:15:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.9.15.7"><i>Sotah</i> 9:17 Note 265</a>; most of the story in greater detail <i>Sotah</i> 9:13–14, Notes 212–218, and the parallels given there in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Horayot 3:5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Horayot.3.5.1">Note 212</a>.</i>.
Those of Bar Pazi and (Bar) [Rebbi]<sup class="footnote-marker">328</sup><i class="footnote">The text of L is in parentheses, the one from B in bracketrs. Since the second family is also called “R. Hoshaia’s” later in L, and the entire story makes sense only if this family was distinguished in learning, the reading from B has to be accepted.</i> Hoshaia went and greeted the Patriarch every day. Those of Rebbi Hoshaia went in first [and left first]<sup class="footnote-marker">329</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 26:30" href="/Exodus.26.30"><i>Ex</i>. 26:30</a>. This argument is a legal argument of R. Immi’s in <i>Šabbat</i> 12:3 (13c l. 60). The Mishnah states that it is a prosecutable sin to write two letters on the Sabbath. Since the Sabbath prohibition is repeated after the instructions for building the Tabernacle (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 31:12-17" href="/Exodus.31.12-17"><i>Ex</i>. 31:12–17</a>; 35:1–3) it is concluded that the forbidden actions on the Sabbath are exactly those which were necessary for the construction of the Tabernacle. R. Immi explains that all logs which formed the walls of the Tabernacle carried two letters and that sides bearing the same letters were put together when the Tabernacle was re-assembled after being transported. This is taken here as a sign that nothing should be changed; marrying into the family of the patriarch cannot erase the advantage conferred by learning.</i>. Those of Bar Pazi went and became related by marriage to the patriarchate. They came and wanted to enter first. They went and asked Rebbi Immi. <i>You shall erect the tabernacle according to its ruling</i><sup class="footnote-marker">330</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 26:30" href="/Exodus.26.30"><i>Ex.</i> 26:30</a>.</i>. Does there exist a ruling for wood? But the log which merited to be put in the North should be put in the North, in the South should be put in the South.
<sup class="footnote-marker">331</sup><i class="footnote">A parallel text (<b>שׁ</b>) is in <i>Šabbat</i> 12:3 (13c l. 62 ff.) The text here is primary; there the story is told as an appendix to the argument of R. Immi which, however, responds not to the question asked about precedence but about Sabbath prohibitions as explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Horayot 3:5:15" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Horayot.3.5.15">Note 329</a>.</i> Two families were in Sepphoris, one of city councillors<sup class="footnote-marker">332</sup><i class="footnote">Greek βουλευταί.</i> and one rural<sup class="footnote-marker">333</sup><i class="footnote">Latin <i>pagani</i>.</i>, who were greeting the Patriarch every day. The councillors went in first and left first. The rural ones went and acquired [knowledge in] Torah. They came and wanted to have precedence. It was asked before Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish asked it from Rebbi Joḥanan. Rebbi Joḥanan went up and preached in Rebbi Benaiah’s house of study<sup class="footnote-marker">334</sup><i class="footnote">The text of B, “of Tiberias” has to be rejected. Not only is the text of L confirmed by the text in <i>Šabbat</i>, but also the remark that he “went up” refers to going from Tiberias below Sea level to Sepphoris high in the mountains but also the entire story is placed at Sepphoris and only there a public ruling was needed.</i>: “But if the bastard was learned and the High Priest ignorant, the learned bastard precedes the ignorant High Priest<sup class="footnote-marker">335</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Horayot 3:5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Horayot.3.5.1">Mishnah 3:9</a>.</i>.” They wanted to say, to be redeemed, for livelihood, and for clothing, but not for the Academy. Rebbi Abun said, even for the Academy. What is the reason? <i>It is more precious than pearls</i><sup class="footnote-marker">336</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Prov</i>.. 3:15.</i>, even than he who enters into the Most Holy [of the Sanctuary.]
